# Macro Intelligence — Overview

_This page is the single synthesis of everything in the wiki. Updated after every ingest._

---

## The Macro Regime

*Last updated: 2026-07-04 | Sources: macro-signals-collect (May 14–Jul 4), fintech-bfsi-digest (May 14–Jul 4), tech-ai-digest (May 14–Jul 4)*

**NEW (July 4 — Jul 2/3 data, US closed Jul 3-4):** The dominant new signal is a clean, single-cause commodity move: **gold and silver rallied sharply — Gold $4,188.57 (+1.25%), Silver $63.18 (+2.48%) — driven by a weak June US nonfarm payrolls report (57K jobs added vs. ~110-115K forecast, unemployment 4.2%)**. This is distinct from the geopolitical/Iran-driven commodity moves that dominated H1 2026 — a pure US-labour-market/Fed-path story. **DXY eased to 100.78 (-0.08%)** as September Fed rate-path odds repriced on the miss. US equities were closed for the holiday weekend; the last print (Dow, July 2) held above 52,000 at 52,900.07 (+1.14%). **India's own settings stayed firmly in "calm, rate-cut-anticipating" mode**: G-Sec 10Y hit a fresh 15-week low of 6.71% (spread ~+222bps to US 10Y), India VIX at a very low 11.98, though paired unusually with a put-heavy Nifty PCR of 1.33 — worth watching for confirmation next week rather than treating as a genuine bearish signal given the holiday-thinned session. **India forex reserves rose only +$0.963Bn to $672.587Bn** (week ended Jun 26) — a sharp deceleration from the prior week's +$20.46Bn surge, confirming that spike was episodic rather than a new accumulation run-rate. See *2026 07 04 macro signals*

The weak NFP print is double-edged for India: a softer US labour market raises the probability of eventual Fed easing (constructive for EM carry and INR), but markets have not yet resolved whether to read it as "bad news is good news" (rate-cut path, risk-on) or a genuine US growth-scare (risk-off) — the muted, not sharp, DXY move suggests the market is still undecided. India's domestic data (G-Sec at a fresh 15-week low) continues to point toward the August MPC cut thesis regardless of how the US read resolves.

**NEW (July 1 — June 30 close):** Global risk appetite reasserted decisively: **Dow closes above 52,000 for the first time (52,319.20, +0.26%)**; S&P 500 7,449.36 (+0.79%); Nasdaq 26,213.72 (+1.52%) — Q2 2026 was a blowout quarter (S&P +14%, Nasdaq +~20%, Dow +12%). The one new friction point: **Iran publicly refused talks with the US "at any level" for the coming days**, even as a US delegation travelled to Qatar — the first direct public setback to ceasefire implementation since the June 19 signing. Brent bounced to $74.28 (+1.99%) off the June 29 ~$72 low; the market read this as noise, not deal collapse. **DXY pulled back to ~101.1-101.2** from its 15-month high (101.6, June 24) but remains on track for a second consecutive monthly gain. India's Nifty PCR shifted from bullish (0.808) to near-neutral (1.02) in a single session, with India VIX ticking up marginally (13.73) — normalisation after the extreme complacency of June 30. A reported India core CPI of 5.1% (up from 4.6%) diverges sharply from the benign ex-gold/silver core reading tracked through June — flagged for verification, as it could complicate the August RBI rate-cut thesis if confirmed. See *2026 07 01 macro signals*

The Iran talks refusal is worth tracking closely: it is the first crack in an otherwise linear ceasefire-implementation narrative that has driven the entire June macro-relief thesis (oil, gold, INR, RBI easing room). Markets are not yet pricing escalation risk — Brent's modest bounce, not a spike, confirms this — but if talks remain stalled into the August MPC window, it would introduce the first meaningful upside risk to India's crude-import-bill assumptions since the June 19 deal signing.

**NEW (June 30 — June 29 close):** **Gold breaks below $4,000 ($3,982.20, -1.40%)** for the first time in weeks as risk-on rotation (small-caps outperforming Big Tech) reduces safe-haven demand. **Brent dipped to ~$72 intraday (lowest since Feb 27); Goldman Sachs cut its Q4 Brent forecast to $80 from $90**, expecting Gulf exports back to pre-war levels by end-July — the supply-normalisation call is now bank consensus. **India forex reserves jumped $20.46Bn in a single week to $702.78B** — the sharpest weekly recovery of 2026, re-crossing the $700B milestone. India G-Sec 10Y holds at ~6.70% (13-week low); India VIX 13.43 (very low) and Nifty PCR 0.808 (bullish) alongside a -1.2 to -1.3% Nifty/Sensex pullback — profit-taking, not a sentiment reversal. SCOTUS blocked the firing of a Fed governor — Fed independence reaffirmed during the Warsh-chair transition. See *2026 06 30 macro signals*

Gold's break below $4,000 and Brent's Goldman-endorsed downgrade both confirm that H1 2026's safe-haven/geopolitical premium is unwinding on an institutional, not just retail, basis. Combined with the $20.46Bn reserve jump, India enters the August MPC window with its strongest three-variable setup of 2026: cheaper energy imports, cheaper gold imports, and a materially larger RBI intervention buffer. The equity pullback, occurring alongside record-low volatility, looks technical rather than fundamental.

**NEW (June 28 — data as of June 27 close, Sunday collection):** WTI $68.86 (-3.74%), Brent $72.60 (-3.84%) — the Iran peace dividend is now maximally expressed in spot prices; India's annualised crude import savings vs. May $111 WTI peak approach $180B. **BIS Annual Economic Report 2026 released** at Basel AGM: headline "Global economic pressure points call for policy discipline" — the global central bank community is framing 2026 as requiring tightening, not easing; India's August RBI cut case is India-specific, not part of a global DM easing wave. **Nikkei -4.15%, KOSPI -5.81%** — Asian tech/semiconductor selloff extending the prior week's Nasdaq -4.6%; semiconductor supply chain anxiety (Samsung/SK Hynix) persists. S&P -0.05%, Sensex +0.14% — US flat, India decoupled. India G-Sec 10Y: 6.70% (13-week low); India-US spread +233bps; Gold $4,040/oz (+1.20%) with COT +228,000 net long. Copper +2.14% ($6.14/lbs) — industrial recovery signal. New WPI series (base 2022-23) effective June 2026 — prior WPI reads becoming series-incomparable going forward. India biofuel: ethanol working (20% blend target near met); now pivoting to next biofuel for residual crude dependency. See *2026 06 28 macro signals*

June 28 is a Sunday, making this a retrospective-data collection. The key regime signal is the simultaneous: (1) oil fully normalised (WTI $68.86, lowest since pre-conflict), and (2) global central bank consensus (BIS) saying "discipline" not "easing." This combination defines India's August MPC moment: the domestic case for a cut is watertight (CPI 3.93% + WTI below $70), but RBI will be cutting against the grain of global central bank orthodoxy — which is fine, but signals the cut cycle will be shallow and data-conditional, not a 2019-style multi-cut sequence.

**NEW (June 27 — June 26 close): WTI $69.40 (-3.51%), Brent <$75 — Persian Gulf exports now ~75% pre-war levels; India's annualised crude savings vs. May $111 peak exceed $170B. India 10Y G-Sec ~6.70% (13-week low) — declining crude + FII debt flows compressing India yields; India-US spread ~+230bps; August RBI rate cut probability rising. Nasdaq weekly -4.6% — Trump admin restricts OpenAI's GPT-5.6 (Sol/Terra/Luna) to "trusted partners" with customer-by-customer approval; de facto AI prior-approval regime established; KOSPI -5.81% (semiconductor supply chain concerns). Bank Nifty +1.69% vs Nifty -0.21% — BFSI accumulation diverging from broader market. WPI-CPI gap: 5.77pp (WPI 9.7% vs CPI 3.93%; core CPI ex-gold/silver: 2.3%) — corporate India margin compression deepening; RBI Pulse Survey: 80%+ firms higher costs, 70% thinner margins. India forex reserves: $672.587B (+$963M WoW). Amazon $13B additional India AI+cloud investment ($48B total 2026-2030; Jassy met Modi in New Delhi). TSMC hiking prices 5-10% across all nodes. CBSE AI curriculum mandate: 28,000 schools, 90-day window, compulsory from 2026-27. India seeking US assurance against AI chip/model cutoffs. See *2026 06 27 macro signals*, *2026 06 27 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 27 tech ai digest***

The June 27 session represents a regime completion point for the oil shock narrative and the opening of a new AI governance risk. WTI at $69.40 (below $70) means India's crude import bill has fully normalised — the June 2026 Iran peace dividend is now maximally expressed in spot prices. Simultaneously, the Trump administration's GPT-5.6 restriction establishes that frontier AI models are now controlled technology subject to government gating — a new sovereign access risk for India's AI ecosystem that replaces Hormuz as the dominant macro uncertainty. The two narratives are inverting simultaneously: India's energy dependency risk is resolved; India's AI infrastructure dependency risk is emerging. India G-Sec at 6.70% (13-week low) is the financial market's clearest signal that the macro relief is real and durable — the bond market is pricing an August RBI rate cut. The WPI-CPI gap (5.77pp) is the residual risk: if input cost easing (via Brent below $70) doesn't filter through to WPI quickly enough, corporate India will stay defensive through H1 FY27.

**NEW (June 26 — June 25 close):** WTI crossed below $70 for the first time since before the US-Iran conflict ($73.05 Brent, <$70 WTI) — India's annualised crude import savings vs. the May $111 peak now exceed $170B. The contradiction: India-bound oil tanker rates surged 897% (ET Energy, June 25), as mine threats and damaged Hormuz infrastructure are raising shipping costs even as cargo prices fall. Net: India's import bill is still materially lower, but supply chain normalisation is not costless. US 10Y fell 9bps to 4.40% — oil deflation compressing US inflation expectations and releasing pressure on the bond market. India-US spread widened to +244bps (from 230bps tightest) as India G-Sec edged to 6.84% while US yields fell. FII debt inflows hit ₹23,600 Cr MTD — the strongest monthly pace in two years — confirming the three-pillar RBI capital playbook (FCNR(B) + G-Sec exemption + LCR pricing) is delivering. Micron Q3 FY2026 beat ($41.5B revenue, EPS $25.11 vs $20.49 est, +22.55%; Q4 guided $50B) materially reversed the AI bubble narrative that had dominated the June 23 selloff. Strait of Hormuz: Oman-Iran joint team now forming to manage navigation framework; toll-free movement assured. RBI Governor Malhotra stated it is "premature to discuss rate hikes" — the clearest signal yet that RBI's next move, if any, remains a cut not a hike. S&P 7,357.49 (▼0.01%), Nasdaq 25,358.60 (▼0.46%); Nikkei 72,366.34 (▲4.61%), Nifty 24,056 (▲0.14%); Bank Nifty bullish engulfing breakout June 25. See *2026 06 26 macro signals*, *2026 06 26 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 26 tech ai digest*

The oil-below-$70 milestone is structurally significant: at this level, India's crude import bill has fully normalised from the May peak. The concurrent tanker rate surge (897%) introduces a friction factor, but shipping costs are transient (insurance risk premium on Hormuz passages normalising as the joint framework takes hold) while the crude price relief is durable. The RBI's Malhotra statement on rate hikes being "premature to discuss" closes off the hawkish tail risk that had been building alongside the DXY 101.6 / Fed hike repricing from two days ago. Combined with CPI at 3.9% and WTI below $70, India's August MPC cut thesis is intact — the only outstanding variable is monsoon and June CPI.

**NEW (June 25 — June 24 close): DXY 101.6 hits 1-year high as markets price 3 Fed hikes before year-end (reversal from 3 cuts expected weeks prior). WTI breaks below $71 — new post-conflict low; Brent $76.47. Gold $4,040 (-1.70%), Silver $61.57 (-5.41%). US-Iran provisional ceasefire framework signed; Bürgenstock talks postponed. S&P 7,358.22 (-0.10%, partial recovery from June 23 selloff); Nasdaq 25,476.64 (-0.43%); DJI 51,848.90 (+0.35%). GIFT Nifty pre-open +0.19%. US 10Y ~4.50% (2-week high); US 2Y ~4.20% (highest since Feb 2025). India G-Sec 6.80%; spread ~230bps; INR 94.67; Kotak range 92.5-97. India CPI May 3.93% (5th consecutive rise, 7bps below 4% target). BIS central bank speeches cluster: PBoC Governor Pan Gongsheng at Lujiazui Forum on China's financial modernisation; SNB news conference. UPI beneficiary name display feature live (RBI fraud-reduction).**

The Fed repricing is the largest macro regime shift since the Iran deal was signed. Markets have moved from pricing 3 rate cuts before year-end to pricing 3 rate hikes — a 150bps swing in implied Fed trajectory. The catalyst: DXY at 1-year high of 101.6 (USD strength reflecting inflation persistence), compounding the AI spending skepticism selloff (June 23 S&P -1.44%). WTI breaking below $71 is paradoxically dovish on inflation — India's crude import savings vs. the May $111 WTI peak now exceed $150B annualised. But the DXY 101.6 signal overrides: higher-for-longer US rates compress EM carry trades, India-US spread (~230bps) is comfortable but not immune, and FII equity outflows (-₹43,044 Cr MTD) continue as a structural drag. The US-Iran provisional ceasefire framework (signed June 24) is one step short of the formal finalisation — Bürgenstock talks postponed due to June 19 logistics gap, creating a 2-4 week rescheduling window. Brent's rebound to $80.57 intraday (on Bürgenstock postponement news) before settling at $76.47 shows the market remains sensitive to deal completion risk. COT: gold ~22,800 net long (not at extremes); crude managed funds recently flipped net-long. See *2026 06 25 macro signals*, *2026 06 25 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 25 tech ai digest*

**NEW (June 24 — June 23 close): AI spending skepticism selloff — S&P -1.44% (7,365), Nasdaq -2.21% (25,587). India decoupled: Nifty +0.37% (24,103), Sensex +0.38%. Iran 60-day oil licence → broad commodity selloff: WTI $73.15 (-0.95%), Gold $4,123 (-1.89%), Silver $62.09 (-5.33%), Copper -2.81%. US 10Y 4.48%; US 2Y 4.20% (highest since Feb 2025). INR 94.74; FII MTD -₹43,044 Cr. India forex $681.61B. India CPI May 3.93%; FTSE India rejig: Lenskart, Tata Capital, Meesho added (~$600M FII passive inflows). Kunal Shah (CRED founder) to lead WhatsApp globally after Meta $900M investment in CRED. BIS Annual Economic Report Chapter III: stablecoins as systemic risk. BrahMos UAE deal signed.**

Bloomberg headlined the June 23 selloff as "Wall Street gets an AI wake-up call" — AI spending skepticism (Amazon, Walmart cutting AI agent spend; Anthropic upgrade trap creating production migration costs) triggered $1.44% S&P decline and $2.21% Nasdaq decline. India's decoupling (+0.37% Nifty on a -1.44% S&P day) is structurally explained: India is not directly in the AI equity multiple compression trade; domestic drivers (RBI June MPC, Iran peace dividend, CPI below 4%) dominate. Iran's 60-day oil licence (US granted Iran right to sell oil internationally — a step toward the supply normalisation trade) triggered the commodity selloff even as the formal deal finalisation remains pending. At WTI $73.15, India's import economics are effectively back to pre-conflict levels — but DXY at 101.6 (reported in June 25 data) and Fed hike repricing are the new macro risks replacing the Hormuz risk. The regime has rotated: from geopolitical oil shock → AI equity multiple compression + Fed-tightening-repricing. See *2026 06 24 macro signals*, *2026 06 24 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 24 tech ai digest*

**NEW (June 23 — June 22 close):** WTI crosses below $75 for the first time since before the US-Iran conflict ($74.30 June 22), while Brent holds at $81.11 — the second leg of the crude normalisation trade is accelerating. The catalyst: a reported US-Iran **60-day roadmap toward a final peace deal** (building on the June 19 Swiss signing), easing residual uncertainty about Hormuz transit resumption timelines. At WTI $74.30, India's import savings vs. the May WTI ~$88 level represent **~$13–14/bbl compression** — translating to $100B+ annualised savings vs. the conflict peak. **India forex reserves >$700B** (held for a third or more consecutive week); the simultaneous crude decline + reserves recovery is a dual macro positive with no precedent in 2026. US equities diverged: S&P 7,621 (▼1.11%) and Nasdaq 26,224 (▼1.11%) pulled back on a risk-off tech session while **DJI +0.30%** (defensive rotation) and **Nikkei +1.96%** (Asian risk-on intact). US 10Y ticked back up to 4.50%; India G-Sec held at ~6.80%; spread ~230bps. **INR 94.49** (stable; trajectory toward 92–94 maintained). **India oil imports rebounded on record Russian crude shipments** — India has structurally shifted crude import composition toward discounted Russian barrels, reducing vulnerability to Gulf corridor disruption even before Hormuz fully normalises. ONGC rebranding as a "gas and oil firm" is the supply-side signal that India's energy strategy is recalibrating toward gas-first. OMCs expected to remain under margin pressure through FY27 as retail fuel price cuts lag the Brent decline. See *2026 06 23 macro signals*

**NEW (June 22 — June 20 close):** Brent breaks below $80 for the first time since the pre-conflict period — $79.20 (June 20), WTI $76.51. The supply normalisation trade is playing out ahead of the formal Hormuz transit normalisation. VP Vance introduced a new communications variable — "skeptical Iran ever closed Hormuz" — but Pentagon confirmed "safe passage intact today" and ~2.9M bbl/day is still transiting. This is US domestic messaging, not deal reversal. India forex reserves **crossed $700B** (3rd consecutive weekly rise; recovering from $681B May low) — a material upgrade in RBI intervention capacity. US equities rallied: S&P 7,500.58 (+1.08%), Nasdaq 26,517.93 (+1.91%), DJI 51,564.70 (+0.14%). Nifty 24,013.10 (June 19); gap-down expected week of June 22. Gold $4,165.28 (lowest since June 11). US 10Y 4.44% (post-FOMC/Warsh easing); India G-Sec 6.80%; spread ~236bps. INR 94.46. **FII equity YTD ₹-2.08L Cr** — the largest sustained equity outflow channel pressuring INR; MTD May 19–Jun 18: ₹-1,025 Cr. COT crude longs at 15-year low bullishness, gold managed funds ~22,800 (down from 173,800 cycle peak). At $79.20 Brent, India's annualised crude import savings vs. May $111 peak exceed $95B. See *2026 06 22 macro signals*, *2026 06 22 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 22 tech ai digest*

The Brent-below-$80 milestone is the supply-normalisation trade's first hard confirmation. The market has moved through three phases: (1) deal-in-anticipation rally (June 9–15: Nifty +7.9%, Brent -20%); (2) sell-the-news (June 19–20: Brent settles at $80 on deal signing); (3) supply-normalisation drift (June 20+: Brent breaking below $80 as real Hormuz transit resumes). At $79.20, India's macro relief is structurally in place — the August RBI rate cut window is fully open (CPI 3.93% + Brent below $80). The FII equity drag (₹-2.08L Cr YTD) is the lingering headwind; but this is global portfolio rebalancing (US AI equity overweight, EM underweight), not India-specific fundamental selling. India's forex reserves crossing $700B — simultaneous with Brent falling — is the clearest sign that the macro regime has shifted from stress to recovery.

**NEW (June 20 — post-deal): US-Iran Peace Deal SIGNED June 19 in Switzerland. Hormuz reopening is live. Sensex 76,802.90 (-0.78%) on June 19 — textbook "sell the news" after 12-day 7.9% rally from June 9 lows. Brent ~$80, WTI $77.33. Gold $4,172.90 (-1.72%) — geopolitical premium in active unwind. INR 94.35 (June 19). India CPI May confirmed 3.93%. Jio Platforms IPO announced at Reliance AGM — potentially India's largest-ever listing. SEBI regulatory revamp (buybacks, AIFs, MFs, bonds) cleared. Amazon/Walmart cutting AI agent spend — enterprise AI ROI not materialising at scale.**

The Iran deal signing is the macro resolution event of 2026. Three simultaneous effects are now in motion: (1) Brent at $80 and falling — annualised India crude import savings vs. May $111 peak exceed $90B; the trajectory toward $70-75 over July-August is the dominant macro tailwind; (2) India August RBI rate cut — CPI 3.93% (below target) + Brent $80 is the dual-positive the MPC needs; the only outstanding question is pace of food inflation normalisation; (3) Jio Platforms IPO — the largest structural capital markets event in India in years, which will increase MSCI India weight and pull $3-5B in passive FII allocation. The "sell the news" on June 19 is healthy — it exhausts the trade-in-anticipation sellers and sets up the next leg of the India rally once Brent data and actual Hormuz vessel transit resumption are observable.

**India WPI-CPI divergence now resolving.** WPI May 9.68% (fuel & power +30.33%) was a mechanical high driven by crude; with Brent below $80 and falling, a sharp WPI reversal is expected by August-September. CPI 3.93% is just below the 4% ceiling. The June-August period should see WPI and CPI converge downward toward 5-6% WPI and 3.5-4% CPI — a benign inflation landing strip for RBI.

**Amazon/Walmart AI agent pullback = important enterprise data point.** Two of the world's largest technology buyers are cutting AI agent spend because ROI isn't materialising at projected cost-per-task ratios. This is a counter-narrative to the frontier AI investment thesis (NVIDIA, Anthropic, OpenAI all benefiting from infrastructure capex) but consistent with the "80% of enterprise AI spend never reaches production" thesis. The two tracks — infrastructure build (real, accelerating) vs. enterprise ROI (slower, contested) — will define the AI trade in 2H 2026. See *2026 06 20 macro signals*, *2026 06 20 tech ai digest*

**NEW (June 17 — post-announcement day):** Brent fell to $78.89 from $83.82 (June 15) — supply-return trade accelerating even before signing. DJI record intraday 52,190 vs S&P/Nasdaq decline (chip selloff continues). India WPI 9.68% = mechanical peak that will reverse as Brent falls. RBI 100% collateral requirement for prop traders — smaller G-Sec desks consolidating. Sarvam AI unicorn ($234M, $1.5B, HCLTech $150M) — India's first full-stack sovereign AI company building foundational models, not just fine-tuning. See *2026 06 17 macro signals*, *2026 06 17 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 17 tech ai digest*

**NEW (June 16): Trump confirms Strait of Hormuz to reopen Friday June 19 after signing of "great peace deal" with Iran. Brent $83.82 (-4.0%), WTI ~$80.00 — lowest since March 2026; -25% from May $111 peak. S&P 7,656.79 (new ATH, past June 1 high of 7,599.96); Nasdaq 26,558.49 (+2.59%); Russell 2000 record high. Nifty 23,853.90 (+0.98%). India VIX 17.02 (+7.85%) — paradox: options hedging June 19 signing execution risk even as equities rallied. INR 94.74 (strengthening). US government orders Anthropic to pull BOTH Mythos AND Fable model series — treated as controlled technology like export-controlled hardware. India WPI May 9.68% (new base year FY22-23; fuel & power +30.33%); CPI May 3.90% — WPI-CPI divergence sharpening. Sarvam AI unicorn ($234M Series B).**

The June 16 session delivered a second consecutive day of Iran deal execution signals, compounding June 15's peace deal confirmation into explicit Hormuz reopening timing. Trump's public statement — "Hormuz to reopen Friday after signing" — removed the residual ambiguity about Hormuz transit resumption timing, which was previously vague in the 14-point draft. Brent's extension to $83.82 (lowest since March) prices this explicitly. The $83.82 level represents ~$6B/month import bill savings vs. the May peak; the $75–80 target post-reopening would expand India's monthly savings to $8–10B/month. August RBI rate cut probability is now the highest it has been in 2026 — CPI 3.90% (below 4% target) plus Brent trajectory firmly downward is the dual-positive the RBI's August MPC needs.

**US government model pullback = controlled technology watershed.** The US ordering Anthropic to pull BOTH the Mythos and Fable lines (not just Mythos, as previously understood) establishes that advanced AI models are now treated as controlled technology similar to export-controlled hardware. This has three immediate India implications: (1) any India enterprise or government agency relying on US frontier AI models faces unilateral supply-chain risk; (2) NITI Aayog reviewing local AI infrastructure is the correct institutional response; (3) Sarvam AI's $234M unicorn raise, timed within days of this episode, captures a new narrative premium — Indian-language, India-sovereign AI as necessity rather than aspiration.

**India VIX paradox (17.02, +7.85%).** Nifty +0.98% but India VIX spiked simultaneously — the options market is hedging June 19 signing execution risk (tail risk if signing is delayed or conditions change), not pricing in post-signing volatility. This is rational: an insurance-style premium for a three-day window. Once June 19 signing executes and Hormuz transit resumes, the VIX premium should unwind rapidly — consistent with the June 15 VIX relief (14.72) once the deal was confirmed.

**WPI-CPI divergence: structural signal emerging.** WPI May 9.68% (vs. 8.26% April) under the new FY22-23 base year — fuel & power +30.33% the primary driver. CPI May 3.90% (vs. 3.48% April) — consumer inflation still well below the 4% midpoint. The divergence signals a supply-side pressure building in producer prices that has not yet fully passed through to consumers. As Brent falls post-Hormuz, WPI should ease in June-August — but if domestic fuel price cuts lag the Brent drop (as is typical for OMC pricing), WPI-CPI convergence will be slower than markets expect. See *2026 06 16 macro signals*, *2026 06 16 fintech bfsi digest*, *2026 06 16 tech ai digest*, *trump*

**NEW (June 15): US-Iran Peace Deal OFFICIALLY CONFIRMED — formal signing ceremony Switzerland June 19. KOSPI +4.63%, Nifty +1.99% extending risk-on. Brent $87.30 (-3.40% further); -21% from May peak. India G-Sec 10Y 6.80%; India-US spread 231bps — tightest in tracking. India CPI May 3.90% (below 4% RBI target). India VIX 14.72 (-5.7%). INR 95.26. China PBoC gold: 2,331.52t — 19th consecutive month. SpaceX SPCX IPO closed ($75B raised, >$2T market cap). Citrini Research: medium-term US equity bullish but 3–4 months elevated volatility ahead (Warsh Fed + AI capex mature leg).**

The Iran deal confirmation is the resolution of the single most consequential macro uncertainty of 2026. From the February 28 war start to June 19 signing: 111 days, ~$20/bbl Brent premium at peak, INR at 96.73 record low, $1.3T chip selloff, 100-day Hormuz near-closure. With formal peace, the unwind is now underway simultaneously across five transmission channels: (1) Brent toward $75–80 = India import bill savings $6–8B/month; (2) INR stabilisation at 94–95 (from 96.73 peak); (3) RBI August rate cut window opened — May CPI at 3.90% (below target) + falling crude removes the Q3 5.9% spike risk from the FY27 CPI path; (4) OMC losses reverse (aviation, LPG downstream sector relief); (5) GCC remittance corridors (Bahrain, Jordan, Kuwait — ~$36B/year from India diaspora) de-risked. The **Citrini Research framing** is critical context: even with the Iran resolution, markets face 3–4 months of elevated volatility from (a) Kevin Warsh's Fed chair confirmation + rate-path recalibration and (b) the AI capex trade's "more mature leg" — momentum concentration remains extreme and drawdowns of 10–15% from highs are expected before a late-summer melt-up. For India: the Iran-deal-driven relief is structural and sustained; the Warsh/Fed/AI-capex volatility is the new rotation risk. See *2026 06 15 macro signals*, *2026 06 15 fintech bfsi digest*, *trump*

**NEW (June 13): US-Iran draft truce formalised in markets — broadest global risk-on rally since conflict began. S&P +1.75% to 7,394.30; Nasdaq +2.54%; Nifty +1.99%; Bank Nifty +3.01%. Brent -4% to ~$89. RBI coordinated three-pillar capital inflow playbook fully confirmed: FCNR(B) FX hedging subsidy + PSU ECB swap + G-Sec tax exemption. Secondary signal: EU-China trade war trajectory building; G7 France June 16-17.**

June 12 was a dual-signal day: the geopolitical and financial capital account tracks reinforced each other simultaneously. The US-Iran draft truce framework circulated through markets on June 12, triggering the sharpest single-session risk-on move of the entire conflict period. S&P at 7,394.30 (+1.75%), Nifty at 23,622.90 (+1.99%), Bank Nifty +3.01% — the Bank Nifty outperformance reflects India equity pricing in both the Brent decline and the RBI capital inflow package's impact on financial sector liquidity. Brent at ~$89 (from $111 May peak = -20%) is the clearest signal that markets are pricing near-term formal deal closure rather than just deescalation talk.

**INR ~85.76** represents a near-unprecedented appreciation in a short period (from ~95 range to 85.76 in weeks). This is the combined output of the Iran peace dividend (Brent -20%) and RBI's 2013 Rajan-style coordinated capital account playbook: (1) FCNR(B) FX hedging subsidy absorbs NRI currency risk so NRIs earn ~7% on dollar deposits = +250bps over US rates; (2) PSU ECB concessional swap; (3) G-Sec capital gains tax exemption for foreign investors. In 2013, the FCNR(B) scheme brought in ~$26B in 2–3 months and moved INR from 68 to 61. The 2026 iteration's results are arriving faster, likely because the Iran peace dividend is compounding the capital inflow benefit. See *2026 06 13 macro signals*, *2026 06 13 fintech bfsi digest*, *trump*

**EU-China trade war building in the background.** G7 France (June 16–17) and EU summit in Brussels are both dedicated to countering China trade practices. EU levies on Chinese EVs, steel, and semiconductors are building toward what one analysis describes as a destination that "may be inevitable." India opportunity: EU trade diversion from China favours India in electronics, EV components, chemicals, and IT services. Watch G7 communiqué language on China.

**NEW (June 12): Trump suspends Iran attacks and signals deal close — Brent falls to $89.23 (WTI $85.94). S&P partial recovery +0.21% to 7,267. Gold ~$4,100 (near Nov 2025 lows). US CPI May 4.2% (beats — Dec Fed hike priced). India G-Sec 10Y falls to ~6.80% (2-month low) on FII debt buying; India-US spread narrows to +226bps. RBI cancels 135 NBFCs; banks raise FCNR(B) rates (2013 Rajan playbook echo).**

The most important June 12 signal is the **geopolitical regime shift**: Trump suspended planned Iran attacks and signalled the US-Iran deal is close. After weeks of multi-front escalation (Iran attacking Bahrain, Jordan, Kuwait on June 10), this is the clearest deescalation signal the market has received. Brent at $89.23 and WTI at $85.94 represent the first sustained sub-$90 prints since the conflict began — unwinding $8–12/bbl of risk premium. If a formal deal closes: Brent targets $75–80, India's import bill drops ~$5–8B/month, INR recovers, RBI gains rate-cut space, and OMC losses reverse. The deal-closing pattern (Trump signals optimism → short reversal → new signal) has repeated multiple times; this is the most concrete signal yet.

**US CPI May 4.2%** — the key data point that anchors the rate narrative. This is the largest monthly jump of 2026; with the Fed now effectively pricing a December rate hike, gold's bear market is structural (higher opportunity cost) not just cyclical. India G-Sec 10Y diverging to 6.80% while US 10Y holds at 4.54% (India-US spread +226bps) shows the RBI capital inflow package (G-Sec tax exemption + FAR expansion + LCR pricing reform) is actively working — foreign buyers are entering India bonds even as US yields stay elevated.

**India domestic credit tightening signals:** Three simultaneous RBI actions — 135 NBFC cancellations, REIT/InvIT lending restriction to listed entities only, and banks' aggressive FCNR(B) rate hikes — signal the RBI is managing the credit supply structure proactively. The FCNR(B) hike echoes the 2013 Rajan playbook (launched FCNR(B) deposits at attractive rates to pull in NRI forex and stabilise INR). Success historically stabilised INR within 6–8 weeks. See *2026 06 12 macro signals*, *trump*

**NEW (June 11): US-Iran conflict becomes multi-front Gulf war — Iran attacks Bahrain, Jordan, Kuwait. S&P 7,267 (▼1.62%), Nasdaq 25,170 (▼1.98%). Gold $4,152 (continued 200-DMA breakdown). India decouples: Nifty only ▼0.12%, INR 94.96 (strengthened). India G-Sec 10Y firms to 7.00%. Brent paradoxically eases to $91 (market pricing eventual normalisation). Fed "4% is the new 2%" narrative takes hold.**

The June 10 session marks a qualitative escalation from Iran-Israel bilateral to a **multi-front Gulf war**: after the US conducted self-defense strikes following an Iranian helicopter downing, Iran attacked Bahrain, Jordan, and Kuwait — three US Gulf Arab allies. Cross-asset correlations rose sharply. Industrials (>3%), Tech and Materials (>2%) led the S&P decline. Yet the risk-asset behaviour was paradoxical: Brent actually eased to $91 despite escalation (markets pricing eventual normalisation), and INR strengthened to 94.96 (possibly RBI-supported), and Nifty fell only 0.12% while global markets sold off heavily — a sharp India decoupling. 

**Gold's 200-DMA breakdown deepens ($4,285 → $4,152)**. Each leg down flushes trend-following longs. At $4,000, cycle-low scenario becomes realistic. Counterweight: COT short reduction + fresh longs building (contrarian signal). The catalyst for a gold snap-back remains a definitive Iran deal.

**"4% is the new 2%"** — commentary circulating that the Fed has effectively abandoned its 2% CPI target; new effective anchor closer to 4%. Direct implication: higher-for-longer US rates, tighter India-US spread (~247bps), and constrained RBI easing space. Goldman's 2-hike call becomes baseline. India G-Sec firmed back to 7.00% (reversing the brief 6.9% trough) as Middle East tension premium rebuilt. **India fuel consumption fell 6.5% MoM in May** — first hard evidence that the war is now visible in demand data, not just sentiment. See *2026 06 11 macro signals*

India found a near-term floor after the June 9 selloff. **Nifty 23,242 (+0.52%)** — bullish hammer candle with 23,070 technical support; if the Iran-Israel ceasefire signal firms, the 23,500–23,550 upside target is plausible within this week. The broader market has been outperforming Big Tech YTD, which structurally confirms the AI equity concentration trade is distributing, not accelerating. For India IT: if Mag 7 multiples compress while S&P 493 holds, India's IT sector (which isn't in Mag 7) sees a mixed signal — less AI demand excitement but less valuation compression risk.

The new driver is the market pricing of **~70% probability of a December Fed rate hike** on the back of continued strong US jobs data. Gold's dual pressure: higher-for-longer US rates + systematic selling = downtrend until Iran deal removes the geopolitical bid need.

**Two shocks landed simultaneously.** Broadcom's Q3 AI chip guidance came in at **$16B vs $17.2B analyst estimates** — a $1.2B miss — and the company narrowed its scope to "chips only" rather than integrated AI systems. Over June 6–8: **Micron −17%, Intel −9%, AMD −12.6%, Broadcom −14%**; ~$1.3T of global semiconductor market cap erased. This hit on top of the US May NFP beat (May 6: 139K jobs vs. 85K consensus), which was already driving higher-for-longer rate fears. The net result: **Nifty fell to 23,123 (▼1.04%, June 9)** — its lowest June 2026 close. **India VIX spiked to 17.09 (+8.2%)**. **Nifty PCR dropped below 0.80** — extreme bearish options positioning, which historically has been a contrarian buy signal around weekly expiry (June 11).

**Gold broke below its 200-day moving average** ($4,356.20) for the first time since October 2023. This is a structural chart signal: trend-following systematic funds will now mechanically reduce gold positions, adding selling momentum on top of the fundamental headwind (higher-for-longer US rates reducing gold's appeal vs. yield-bearing assets). The gold selloff has now been running for ~4 weeks (peak ~$4,700 → current $4,356 = −7.5%).

**Iran partial ceasefire — oil relief signal.** Iran announced it ended military operations against Israel — **Brent jumped +4% to ~$94/bbl**. This is the most concrete geopolitical deescalation signal since the Hormuz crisis began 100+ days ago. If confirmed and the Strait reopens to normal traffic, the single largest driver of India's macro stress (energy import bill) could ease materially. Brent at $75–80 is the "Iran deal" scenario that unlocks RBI rate cuts, INR recovery, and India corporate margin relief. Watch: Hormuz traffic data and Iranian official statements.

**India: beat on growth, worse on price.** GDP Q4 FY26 at **7.8%** beat vs. consensus. But RBI revised FY27 CPI to **5.1% full-year** (Q3 spike to 5.9% driven by El Niño monsoon risk + LPG + base metals) and cut GDP to **6.6%** (from 6.9%). The combination is stagflationary: below-trend growth with above-target inflation limits RBI's easing space. Q3 CPI at 5.9% — if realised — would likely force a rate hold or hike vs. the market's cut expectations. See *2026 06 09 macro signals*, *2026 06 09 fintech bfsi digest*

**India-specific signals (June 8):** (1) **ATMs running out of cash** — Filter Coffee newsletter flags cash availability stress, likely driven by fuel demand surge + RBI currency management lag; a first in recent years. (2) **LPG hiked ₹29/cylinder** — the fifth fuel hike since the US-Iran war began; rural households (LPG is the primary cooking fuel) face compounding cost pressure. (3) **ICRA projects FY27 bank credit growth at 11.0–11.7% YoY** (credit expansion ₹23.5–25.0 trillion) — a significant deceleration from FY26's 16.2% pace, driven by funding cost pressures, deposit repricing, and macro headwinds. (4) **Nuclear energy private sector sops under consideration** — India govt considering incentives for private sector nuclear energy participation, first significant shift from government-only model. (5) **Indus Waters Treaty ruling deepens India-Pakistan rift** — post-Operation Sindoor, IWT legal dispute adds another diplomatic pressure layer. **FII equity net sellers at −₹3,912 Cr MTD.** See *2026 06 08 macro signals*

India raised fuel prices a **third time in 10 days** (petrol ~₹101+/L) as of May 23. Structural oil dependency debate now at policy level.

**RBI declared record ₹2.87 lakh crore dividend** (May 23) to the government as a fiscal buffer against war shock — the largest payout ever, driven by forex gains and investment income. Simultaneously, RBI explicitly stated it is **not in favour of rate hikes to defend the rupee**; inflation, not currency, will guide rate decisions. Arvind Panagariya's public advice — *"100 is just a number; let rupee depreciate or reserves will bleed out"* — signals elite consensus forming around managed depreciation.

India-US spread: **~243bps** (tightest in 2 months). Germany Bund retreating from May 2011 highs.
